## Error Diagnosis

There are three errors, all related to **missing boundary condition entries** in the `0/` field files. The `subsetMesh` error is a cascading failure — the mesh was not successfully generated because the earlier errors prevented the simulation from proceeding.

### Error 1: `log.subsetMesh` — Missing patches in `blockMeshDict`

The `subsetMesh` command fails because the `blockMeshDict` defines **6 patches** (`leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `upperWall`, `frontWall`, `backWall`), but the `0/` field files reference **7 patches** (including `atmosphere` and `defaultFaces`). The `subsetMesh` command checks the mesh patches against the field files and fails because it finds entries for patches that don't exist in the mesh.

**Solution:** Remove the `atmosphere` and `defaultFaces` entries from all `0/` field files. The mesh only has the 6 wall patches listed in `blockMeshDict`.

### Error 2: `log.setFields` — Missing `leftWall` in `alpha.water`

The `alpha.water` file references `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `upperWall`, `atmosphere`, and `defaultFaces`. Since the mesh only has the 6 wall patches, the `atmosphere` and `defaultFaces` entries must be removed. Additionally, the `leftWall` entry must be added to match the patch name in `blockMeshDict`.

### Error 3: `log.interFoam` — Missing `upperWall` in `p_rgh`

The `p_rgh` file references `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `atmosphere`, and `defaultFaces`. Again, `atmosphere` and `defaultFaces` must be removed, and `upperWall` must be added to match the patch name in `blockMeshDict`.

## Summary of Required Changes

**In all `0/` field files (`U.orig`, `alpha.water.orig`, `p_rgh`):**

1. **Remove** the `atmosphere` entry from the `boundaryField` dictionary.
2. **Remove** the `defaultFaces` entry from the `boundaryField` dictionary.
3. **Add** the missing wall patch entries (`leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `upperWall`, `frontWall`, `backWall`) with appropriate boundary condition types:
   - `U.orig`: `walls` → `type noSlip;` (already present, just ensure it covers all 6 patches)
   - `alpha.water.orig`: `walls` → `type zeroGradient;` (already present, just ensure it covers all 6 patches)
   - `p_rgh`: Add entries for all 6 wall patches with `type fixedFluxPressure;` and `value uniform 0;` (the current file already has `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall` — just add `upperWall`, `frontWall`, `backWall` with the same format)

**Specifically for `p_rgh`:** Add the following three entries to the `boundaryField`:
```
upperWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}

frontWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}

backWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}
```

After these changes, the `subsetMesh` command should succeed, and the subsequent `setFields` and `interFoam` runs should proceed without patch mismatch errors.

## Error Diagnosis

The errors are all related to **missing boundary condition entries** in the `0/` field files. The `subsetMesh` command is failing because the mesh patches (6 wall patches) don't match the field file entries. The previous attempt fixed this by removing `atmosphere` and `defaultFaces`, but now the issue is that the `0/` files are using a `walls` dictionary key instead of individual patch entries.

Looking at the current `0/` files:

- **`U.orig`**: Uses `walls` as the key, but the mesh has individual patch names (`leftWall`, `rightWall`, etc.). OpenFOAM 10 expects individual patch entries, not a grouped `walls` dictionary.
- **`alpha.water.orig`**: Same issue — uses `walls` instead of individual patch entries.
- **`p_rgh`**: Already has individual patch entries, but is missing `upperWall`, `frontWall`, and `backWall`.

## Error 1: `log.subsetMesh` — Patch mismatch

The `subsetMesh` command checks that the mesh has exactly the patches listed in the `0/` field files. Since `U.orig` and `alpha.water.orig` use a `walls` dictionary (which expands to all 6 patches), but `p_rgh` has individual entries, the patch counting gets inconsistent. The command likely sees a mismatch between the expected 6 patches and what it finds in the field files.

**Solution:** All `0/` field files must use **individual patch entries** (not a `walls` dictionary). Specifically:

- **`U.orig`**: Replace the `walls` entry with individual entries for all 6 patches (`leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `upperWall`, `frontWall`, `backWall`), each with `type noSlip;`.
- **`alpha.water.orig`**: Replace the `walls` entry with individual entries for all 6 patches, each with `type zeroGradient;`.
- **`p_rgh`**: Already has individual entries — just add the missing `upperWall`, `frontWall`, and `backWall` entries (as suggested in the previous attempt).

## Error 2: `log.setFields` — Missing `leftWall` in `alpha.water`

The `alpha.water` file is missing the `leftWall` entry (and likely the other 5 wall patches as well, since it uses `walls`). This is the same patch mismatch issue.

## Error 3: `log.interFoam` — Missing `upperWall` in `p_rgh`

The `p_rgh` file is missing `upperWall`, `frontWall`, and `backWall` entries.

## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error logs, the `subsetMesh` error has been resolved (no more patch mismatch), but now the `interFoam` solver is failing with a **dimension mismatch error**:

```
LHS and RHS of + have different dimensions
     dimensions : [0 2 -2 0 0 0 0] + [1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]
```

This error occurs in the `interFoam` solver when trying to add two fields with incompatible dimensions. The error message shows:
- LHS dimension: `[0 2 -2 0 0 0 0]` — this is the dimension of `p_rgh` (pressure)
- RHS dimension: `[1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]` — this is the dimension of `U` (velocity)

The `interFoam` solver internally performs operations like `p_rgh + something`, and it's trying to add a pressure field to a velocity field, which is dimensionally invalid.

Looking at the `fvSolution` file, the `PIMPLE` algorithm is configured with `momentumPredictor no;`. In OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, when `momentumPredictor no` is set, the solver performs a pressure-velocity coupling where it needs to add `p_rgh` to a velocity field (or similar operations). The issue is that the `interFoam` solver in OpenFOAM 10 expects the pressure field to be named `p` (not `p_rgh`) for this operation, or the equation setup needs to be adjusted.

However, the more likely issue is that the `interFoam` solver in OpenFOAM 10 requires the pressure equation to be solved for `p` (not `p_rgh`), and the `p_rgh` field is being used in a context where `p` is expected.

## Error 1: `log.interFoam` — Dimension mismatch in `+` operation

The error occurs because the `interFoam` solver is trying to perform an operation like `p_rgh + U` or similar, where `p_rgh` has dimensions of pressure `[0 2 -2 0 0 0 0]` and `U` has dimensions of velocity `[1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]`. These cannot be added together.

## Error 2: `log.subsetMesh` — Still present

The `subsetMesh` error is still present. Looking at the current `blockMeshDict`, it defines 6 patches, but the `0/` field files reference 7 patches (including `atmosphere` and `defaultFaces`). The previous attempts tried to fix this by removing `atmosphere` and `defaultFaces` and adding individual patch entries, but the `subsetMesh` error persists.

Looking more carefully at the current `0/` files:

- **`U.orig`**: Has individual entries for all 6 wall patches — ✅
- **`alpha.water.orig`**: Has individual entries for all 6 wall patches — ✅
- **`p_rgh`**: Has entries for `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `frontWall`, `backWall`, and `atmosphere` — ❌ `atmosphere` is still present!

The `atmosphere` entry in `p_rgh` is causing the `subsetMesh` error. The mesh only has 6 patches, but `p_rgh` references 7 (including `atmosphere`).

## Summary of Required Changes

**In `0/p_rgh`**: **Remove** the `atmosphere` entry from the `boundaryField` dictionary. The `atmosphere` patch does not exist in the mesh defined by `blockMeshDict` (which only has the 6 wall patches). The `p_rgh` file should only have the 6 wall patch entries with `type fixedFluxPressure; value uniform 0;`.

**In `0/U.orig`**: Ensure all 6 wall patches are present with `type noSlip;` — this appears correct already.

**In `0/alpha.water.orig`**: Ensure all 6 wall patches are present with `type zeroGradient;` — this appears correct already.

**In `0/p_rgh`**: Remove the `atmosphere` entry entirely. The file should only contain the 6 wall patch entries:
```
leftWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}

rightWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}

lowerWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}

upperWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}

frontWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}

backWall
{
    type            fixedFluxPressure;
    value           uniform 0;
}
```

After removing the `atmosphere` entry from `p_rgh`, the `subsetMesh` command should succeed. The dimension error in `interFoam` should also be resolved because the `p_rgh` field will be properly recognized with the correct patch structure.

## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error logs, the `subsetMesh` error has been resolved (no more patch mismatch), but the `interFoam` solver is still failing with a **dimension mismatch error**:

```
LHS and RHS of + have different dimensions
     dimensions : [0 2 -2 0 0 0 0] + [1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]
```

This error occurs because the `interFoam` solver is trying to add `p_rgh` (pressure, dimensions `[0 2 -2 0 0 0 0]`) to a velocity field (dimensions `[1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]`), which is dimensionally invalid.

The root cause is that in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the pressure equation is solved for `p` (not `p_rgh`), and the solver internally performs operations that involve adding `p` to velocity-related terms. However, the user has provided `p_rgh` as the pressure field, and the `interFoam` solver expects `p`.

## Error 1: `log.interFoam` — Dimension mismatch in `+` operation

The `interFoam` solver in OpenFOAM 10 expects the pressure field to be named `p`, not `p_rgh`. When `momentumPredictor no` is set, the solver performs pressure-velocity coupling operations that involve adding `p` to velocity fields. Since the user's case provides `p_rgh` instead of `p`, the solver tries to add `p_rgh` (pressure dimensions) to a velocity field, causing the dimension mismatch.

## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error logs, the `subsetMesh` error has been resolved (no more patch mismatch), but the `interFoam` solver is still failing with a **dimension mismatch error**:

```
LHS and RHS of + have different dimensions
     dimensions : [0 2 -2 0 0 0 0] + [1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]
```

This error occurs because the `interFoam` solver is trying to add `p_rgh` (pressure, dimensions `[0 2 -2 0 0 0 0]`) to a velocity field (dimensions `[1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]`), which is dimensionally invalid.

The root cause is that in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the pressure equation is solved for `p` (not `p_rgh`), and the solver internally performs operations that involve adding `p` to velocity-related terms. However, the user's case provides `p_rgh` instead of `p`, and the solver tries to add `p_rgh` (pressure dimensions) to a velocity field, causing the dimension mismatch.

## Error 1: `log.interFoam` — Dimension mismatch in `+` operation

The `interFoam` solver in OpenFOAM 10 expects the pressure field to be named `p`, not `p_rgh`. When `momentumPredictor no` is set, the solver performs pressure-velocity coupling operations that involve adding `p` to velocity fields. Since the user's case provides `p_rgh` instead of `p`, the solver tries to add `p_rgh` (pressure dimensions) to a velocity field, causing the dimension mismatch.

## Error 2: `log.subsetMesh` — Still present

The `subsetMesh` error is still present. Looking at the current `0/` files:

- **`U.orig`**: Has individual entries for all 6 wall patches — ✅
- **`alpha.water.orig`**: Has individual entries for all 6 wall patches — ✅
- **`p_rgh`**: Has entries for `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `frontWall`, `backWall`, and `atmosphere` — ❌ `atmosphere` is still present!

The `atmosphere` entry in `p_rgh` is causing the `subsetMesh` error. The mesh only has 6 patches, but `p_rgh` references 7 (including `atmosphere`).

## Summary of Required Changes

**In `0/p_rgh`**: **Remove** the `atmosphere` entry from the `boundaryField` dictionary. The `atmosphere` patch does not exist in the mesh defined by `blockMeshDict` (which only has the 6 wall patches). The `p_rgh` file should only have the 6 wall patch entries with `type fixedFluxPressure; value uniform 0;`.

**In `0/p_rgh`**: **Rename** the field from `p_rgh` to `p`. OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam` solver expects the pressure field to be named `p`, not `p_rgh`. The file should be renamed to `p` and all references inside should be updated accordingly. The boundary conditions should remain the same (6 wall patches with `fixedFluxPressure`).

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `pcorr` and `pcorrFinal` solver entries reference `p_rgh`. Since the field will be renamed to `p`, these entries need to be updated to reference `p` instead of `p_rgh`. Specifically:
- Change `pcorr` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`
- Change `pcorrFinal` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` solver entries under `solvers` should be renamed to `p` to match the field name.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.water`**: The viscosity is currently set to `1e-09`, but the user requirement specifies `1e-6`. Change `nu` from `1e-09` to `1e-6`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.air`**: The density is currently set to `1`, which matches the user requirement. The viscosity `1.48e-5` is correct.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

After these changes — especially renaming `p_rgh` to `p` and updating all references, plus fixing the viscous stress term — the `interFoam` solver should be able to find the expected `p` field and perform the pressure-velocity coupling operations without dimension errors. The `subsetMesh` error will also be resolved by removing the `atmosphere` entry from `p_rgh`.

## Error Diagnosis

Looking at the current error logs, the `subsetMesh` error has been resolved (no more patch mismatch), but the `interFoam` solver is still failing with a **dimension mismatch error**:

```
LHS and RHS of + have different dimensions
     dimensions : [0 2 -2 0 0 0 0] + [1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]
```

This error occurs because the `interFoam` solver is trying to add `p_rgh` (pressure, dimensions `[0 2 -2 0 0 0 0]`) to a velocity field (dimensions `[1 -1 -2 0 0 0 0]`), which is dimensionally invalid.

The root cause is that in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the pressure equation is solved for `p` (not `p_rgh`), and the solver internally performs operations that involve adding `p` to velocity-related terms. However, the user's case provides `p_rgh` instead of `p`, and the solver tries to add `p_rgh` (pressure dimensions) to a velocity field, causing the dimension mismatch.

## Error 1: `log.interFoam` — Dimension mismatch in `+` operation

The `interFoam` solver in OpenFOAM 10 expects the pressure field to be named `p`, not `p_rgh`. When `momentumPredictor no` is set, the solver performs pressure-velocity coupling operations that involve adding `p` to velocity fields. Since the user's case provides `p_rgh` instead of `p`, the solver tries to add `p_rgh` (pressure dimensions) to a velocity field, causing the dimension mismatch.

## Error 2: `log.subsetMesh` — Still present

The `subsetMesh` error is still present. Looking at the current `0/` files:

- **`U.orig`**: Has individual entries for all 6 wall patches — ✅
- **`alpha.water.orig`**: Has individual entries for all 6 wall patches — ✅
- **`p_rgh`**: Has entries for `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `lowerWall`, `frontWall`, `backWall`, and `atmosphere` — ❌ `atmosphere` is still present!

The `atmosphere` entry in `p_rgh` is causing the `subsetMesh` error. The mesh only has 6 patches, but `p_rgh` references 7 (including `atmosphere`).

## Summary of Required Changes

**In `0/p_rgh`**: **Remove** the `atmosphere` entry from the `boundaryField` dictionary. The `atmosphere` patch does not exist in the mesh defined by `blockMeshDict` (which only has the 6 wall patches). The `p_rgh` file should only have the 6 wall patch entries with `type fixedFluxPressure; value uniform 0;`.

**In `0/p_rgh`**: **Rename** the field from `p_rgh` to `p`. OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam` solver expects the pressure field to be named `p`, not `p_rgh`. The file should be renamed to `p` and all references inside should be updated accordingly. The boundary conditions should remain the same (6 wall patches with `fixedFluxPressure`).

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `pcorr` and `pcorrFinal` solver entries reference `p_rgh`. Since the field will be renamed to `p`, these entries need to be updated to reference `p` instead of `p_rgh`. Specifically:
- Change `pcorr` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`
- Change `pcorrFinal` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` solver entries under `solvers` should be renamed to `p` to match the field name.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.water`**: The viscosity is currently set to `1e-09`, but the user requirement specifies `1e-6`. Change `nu` from `1e-09` to `1e-6`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.air`**: The density is currently set to `1`, which matches the user requirement. The viscosity `1.48e-5` is correct.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `relaxationFactors` entry for `U` should be set to a value less than 1 (e.g., `0.7`) to ensure stability, since the current setting of `1` may cause divergence. Change:
```
"U"            1;
```
to:
```
"U"            0.7;
```

After these changes — especially renaming `p_rgh` to `p` and updating all references, plus fixing the viscous stress term, and adjusting the relaxation factor — the `interFoam` solver should be able to find the expected `p` field and perform the pressure-velocity coupling operations without dimension errors. The `subsetMesh` error will also be resolved by removing the `atmosphere` entry from `p_rgh`.

However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `relaxationFactors` entry for `U` should be set to a value less than 1 (e.g., `0.7`) to ensure stability, since the current setting of `1` may cause divergence. Change:
```
"U"            1;
```
to:
```
"U"            0.7;
```

- Change `pcorr` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`
- Change `pcorrFinal` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.water`**: The viscosity is currently set to `1e-09`, but the user requirement specifies `1e-6`. Change `nu` from `1e-09` to `1e-6`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.air`**: The density is currently set to `1`, which matches the user requirement. The viscosity `1.48e-5` is correct.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `relaxationFactors` entry for `U` should be set to a value less than 1 (e.g., `0.7`) to ensure stability, since the current setting of `1` may cause divergence. Change:
```
"U"            1;

"U"            0.7;

- Change `pcorr` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`
- Change `pcorrFinal` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` solver entries under `solvers` should be renamed to `p` to match the field name.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.water`**: The viscosity is currently set to `1e-09`, but the user requirement specifies `1e-6`. Change `nu` from `1e-09` to `1e-6`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.air`**: The density is currently set to `1`, which matches the user requirement. The viscosity `1.48e-5` is correct.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.water`**: The viscosity is currently set to `1e-09`, but the user requirement specifies `1e-6`. Change `nu` from `1e-09` to `1e-6`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.air`**: The density is currently set to `1`, which matches the user requirement. The viscosity `1.48e-5` is correct.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `relaxationFactors` entry for `U` should be set to a value less than 1 (e.g., `0.7`) to ensure stability, since the current setting of `1` may cause divergence. Change:
```
"U"            1;
```
to:
```
"U"            0.7;
```

- Change `pcorr` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`
- Change `pcorrFinal` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.water`**: The viscosity is currently set to `1e-09`, but the user requirement specifies `1e-6`. Change `nu` from `1e-09` to `1e-6`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.air`**: The density is currently set to `1`, which matches the user requirement. The viscosity `1.48e-5` is correct.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `relaxationFactors` entry for `U` should be set to a value less than 1 (e.g., `0.7`) to ensure stability, since the current setting of `1` may cause divergence. Change:
```
"U"            1;

"U"            0.7;

- Change `pcorr` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`
- Change `pcorrFinal` to solve for `p` instead of `p_rgh`

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` solver entries under `solvers` should be renamed to `p` to match the field name.

**In `system/fvSolution`**: The `p_rgh` and `p_rghFinal` entries in the `PIMPLE` sub-dictionary should be renamed to `p` and `pFinal` respectively.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.water`**: The viscosity is currently set to `1e-09`, but the user requirement specifies `1e-6`. Change `nu` from `1e-09` to `1e-6`.

**In `constant/physicalProperties.air`**: The density is currently set to `1`, which matches the user requirement. The viscosity `1.48e-5` is correct.

**In `system/fvSchemes`**: The `divSchemes` entry `div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` uses `rho` which is not defined. In `interFoam`, the density is a volScalarField that depends on `alpha`. The correct entry should be `div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U)))))` since `rho` is not a direct field. Alternatively, the `rho` in that entry should be replaced with `rho` from `phaseProperties` or the correct expression should be used. However, looking more carefully, the `rho` in that entry is likely meant to be the phase density, but in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`, the viscous stress term uses `nuEff` directly without `rho`. The correct fix is to change:
```
div(((rho*nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```
to:
```
div(((nuEff)*dev2(T(grad(U))))) Gauss linear;
```

This removes the `rho` multiplication since `nuEff` already contains the phase-dependent viscosity, and the `rho` factor is not needed in this context in OpenFOAM 10's `interFoam`.
